The Sunnah as a Source of Law: Its Rank, Function, and Dependence on the Qur'an
Explaining rank, function, and dependence of Sunnah on Qur'an

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the rank of the Sunnah relative to the Qur'an and identify its functions of bayan, idah, taqyid, and tadaaruk, and apply the principles of reconciling, preponderating, and abrogating conflicting hadith.

Core Idea
The Sunnah explains the Qur'an and is dependent on it, but also independently establishes rulings like the grandmother's inheritance.

In this passage from Mustafa al-Zarqa's introduction to fiqh, we explore how the Sunnah functions as a legislative source. The author clarifies its rank, its dual nature of independence and dependence, and the methods scholars use when hadith conflict. Understanding this relationship is foundational for any mufti applying Sunnah in ifta.

Guided Path
1
Identify the functions of the Sunnah
List the four functions mentioned: bayan (explanation), idah (clarification), taqyid (restriction), and tadaaruk (supplementation).
These show how the Sunnah relates to the Qur'an.
2
Understand the dual nature of the Sunnah
Note the independence (e.g., grandmother's inheritance) and dependence (rooted in Qur'anic principles and general rules).
The Sunnah is not entirely separate but emerges from Qur'anic objectives.
3
Conflict resolution methodology
Recognize the sequence: first reconciliation (tawfiq), then preponderance (tarjih), then abrogation (naskh).
This hierarchy is crucial when facing apparent contradictions.
4
Authenticity requirement
Only authentically established (thabit) hadith are accepted; scholars have detailed conditions.
This filters weak or fabricated reports.
5
Practical implication for ifta
Consider how a mufti would apply this hierarchy when deriving a ruling from Sunnah alongside Qur'an.
Always start with Qur'an, then Sunnah, and resolve conflicts methodically.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثاني : مصادر الفقه الإسلامي
ذلك الحديث المنقول ؛ فيقال عندئذ جاء في الحديث (كذا) ولكن السنة على (كذا).
وفي هذه الحال إذا كان كل من الحديث والسنة صحيح الثبوت يلجأ العلماء إلى التوفيق بين الحديث والسنة إن أمكن، أو إلى ترجيح أحدهما بأسباب مُرَجُحة إن لم يمكن التوفيق، كما إذا تعارض حديثان من قول الرسول صحيحا الثبوت فإنهما يعتبر أحدهما ناسخاً للآخر، فيبحث عن الناسخ والمنسوخ منهما.
والسنة تلي الكتاب رتبة في مصدريَّة ،التشريع، من حيث إنَّ بها بيان مجمله، وإيضاح مشكله وتقييد مطلقه وتدارك ما لم يذكر فيه.
فالسنة مصدر تشريعي مستقل من جهة، لأنها قد يَرِدُ فيها من الأحكام ما لم يرد في القرآن كميراث الجدة، فقد ثبت أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم حكم بتوريث جدة المتوفى سدس المال ولكن السنة من جهة أخرى يلحظ فيها معنى التبعية للقرآن لأنها، علاوة على كونها بياناً وإيضاحاً له، تخرج عن مبادئه وقواعده العامة حتى فيما تقرره من الأحكام التي لم يرد ذكرها في القرآن فمرجع السنة في الحقيقة إلى نصوص القرآن لا وقواعده العامة .
والسنة بصورة عامة ضرورية لفهم الكتاب لا يمكن أن يستغنى عنها في فهمه وتطبيقه وإن كان فيها ما لا يتوقف عليه فهم الكتاب هذا التوقف .
هذا وبعد أن أصبحت السنة تنقل نقلاً بالرواية، لانقضاء عصر الرسالة، وانقطاع مشافهة الرسول بوفاته عليه السلام، لا يقبل منها في تشريع الأحكام الفقهية إلا ما كان صحيح الثبوت بشرائط معينة شديدة.
وقد تكفل علماء السنة بتمييز مراتب الأحاديث النبوية في الثبوت.
Chapter Two: Sources of Islamic Jurisprudence. That transmitted hadith; then it is said: it came in the hadith (such) but the Sunnah is upon (such). In this situation, if both the hadith and the Sunnah are authentically established, scholars resort to reconciliation between the hadith and the Sunnah if possible, or to giving precedence to one over the other with preponderating reasons if reconciliation is not possible, just as if two sayings of the Prophet, both authentically established, conflict, then one is considered abrogating the other, so one searches for the abrogating and abrogated among them. The Sunnah follows the Book in rank as a source of legislation, in that by it its summary is explained, its ambiguous clarified, its absolute restricted, and what is not mentioned in it is supplemented. The Sunnah is an independent legislative source from one aspect, because it may contain rulings not found in the Qur'an, such as the inheritance of the grandmother, for it is established that the Prophet (peace be upon him) ruled that the grandmother of the deceased inherits one-sixth of the wealth. But from another aspect, the Sunnah has a sense of dependence on the Qur'an, for besides being an explanation and clarification of it, it emanates from its principles and general rules even in what it establishes of rulings not mentioned in the Qur'an. So the reference of the Sunnah in reality is to the texts of the Qur'an [and] its general rules. The Sunnah in general is necessary for understanding the Book; it cannot be dispensed with in understanding and applying it, although there are parts of it for which understanding the Book does not depend [on them fully]. This, and after the Sunnah came to be transmitted by narration, with the end of the prophetic era and the cessation of direct speech of the Messenger by his death (peace be upon him), only what is authentically established under strict conditions is accepted in the legislation of juristic rulings. The scholars of hadith have undertaken to distinguish the ranks of prophetic hadith in terms of authenticity.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage discusses the Sunnah as a source of Islamic law. It opens by noting how conflicts between hadith and Sunnah are resolved: first reconciliation, then preponderance, then abrogation. It then clarifies the rank of Sunnah as secondary to the Qur'an, describing its functions: clarifying the ambiguous, restricting absolute, and supplementing. The author highlights the dual nature of Sunnah: independent in that it can establish rulings not in Qur'an (like grandmother's inheritance), yet dependent on Qur'an's principles. The passage stresses the necessity of Sunnah for understanding the Qur'an. Finally, it outlines the requirement of authentic transmission due to the closing of revelation.

Key Terms
السنة (al-Sunnah): The sayings, actions, and tacit approvals of the Prophet Muhammad, serving as a source of Islamic law.
النسخ والترجيح (al-naskh wa al-tarjih): Abrogation and preponderance: methods to resolve contradiction between apparently conflicting proofs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Sunnah is both independent in establishing rulings not found in the Qur'an and dependent on the Qur'an's principles; understanding this balance is essential for sound ijtihad.

Ijma': Definition, Authority, and Evidentiary Basis
Defining Ijma', proving its authority, and explaining its basis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Ijma' according to the Hanafi school, identify the primary textual evidence for its authority, and explain why Ijma' must be based on a legal proof.

Core Idea
Ijma' is the consensus of all mujtahids of an era, binding as a source after the Sunnah, and it must be rooted in a Shar'i proof.

In this passage, Mustafa al-Zarqa introduces Ijma' as the third fundamental source of Islamic law. He defines it precisely, establishes its rank below the Quran and Sunnah, and marshals Quranic and hadith evidence to prove its authority. He also addresses a critical nuance: consensus cannot be mere agreement; it must be anchored in a valid legal proof. This lesson unpacks the definition, the evidence, and the essential condition of being proof-based.

Guided Path
1
Define Ijma' linguistically and technically
Break down the definition: who are the mujtahids? what does 'agreement of an era' entail? Note that Hanafis require the agreement of all mujtahids of the era.
The text explicitly includes Companions and later generations.
2
Identify the rank of Ijma' among sources
According to the text, Ijma' is a strong proof (hujja) and follows the Sunnah in rank.
It is the third source after Quran and Sunnah.
3
Examine the textual evidence for Ijma's authority
The text cites Quran 4:115 and the hadith 'My community will not unite upon error', along with other hadiths. Understand how these prove authority through mutual reinforcement.
The author emphasizes that these texts collectively constitute sufficient evidence.
4
Analyze the condition that Ijma' must be based on a proof
Even if the proof is not transmitted with the consensus, the consensus must have a basis. Why is this necessary? To avoid whimsical agreement.
This ensures Ijma' is not arbitrary but rooted in the sources.
5
Apply this understanding to ascertaining Ijma'
If later scholars want to verify an Ijma', they must search for the underlying proof.
This is a practical implication for muftis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل (۳) المصادر الأساسية للفقه
المبحث الثالث: الإجماع
٤/٣ - الإجماع هو اتفاق الفقهاء المجتهدين في عصر على حكم. ولا فرق بين أن يكون هؤلاء المتفقون من فقهاء صحابة الرسول عليه الصلاة والسلام بعد وفاته أو من الطبقات التي جاءت بعدهم. والإجماع حُجَّة قوية في إثبات الأحكام الفقهية، ومصدر يلي السنة في الرتبة .
ودليل اعتباره في هذه المكانة من مصدرية التشريع مجموعة آيات وأحاديث تدل على اعتبار إجماع الكلمة من أهل العلم والرأي حجة. فمن تلك الأدلة على اعتبار الإجماع قول الله تبارك وتعالى: ﴿وَمَن يُشَاقِقِ الرَّسُولَ مِنْ بَعْدِ مَا نَبَيَّنَ لَهُ الْهُدَى وَيَتَّبِعْ غَيْرَ سَبِيلِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ نُوَلِهِ مَا تَوَلَّى وَنُصْلِهِ جَهَنَّمَ وَسَاءَتْ مَصِيرًا ﴾ سورة النساء / ١١٥، وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «لا تجتمع أمتي على الضلالة) (۱) وفي معناه أحاديث كثيرة. فبتضافرها بعضها مع بعض ومع الآيات القرآنية التي تأمر بلزوم الجماعة وعدم الانشقاق عنها، تؤلف دليلاً كافياً في حجية الإجماع في إثبات الأحكام.
والإجماع في ذاته إذا انعقد على حكم لا بد أن يكون مستنداً إلى دليل فيه، وإن لم ينقل الدليل معه، إذ لا يعقل أن تجتمع كلمة علماء الأمة الموثوق بهم تشهياً بلا دليل شرعي. ولذلك كان الإجماع إذا أراد المتأخرون معرفته إنما يبحثون عن (1) أخرجه أبو داود من حديث أبي مالك الأشعري (٤٢٥٣)، والترمذي من حديث ابن عمر ( ٢١٦٧) وقال : غريب من هذا الوجه وابن ماجه من حديث أنس (٣٩٥٠) بإسناد ضعيف، وبالجملة فالحديث كما قال الحافظ في التلخيص ١٤١/٣: حديث مشهور له طرق كثيرة، لا يخلو واحد منها من مقال وقال السخاوي في المقاصد ص ٤٦٠ : وبالجملة فهو حديث مشهور ،المتن ذو أسانيد كثيرة، وشواهد الحسنة متعددة في المرفوع وغيره .
Chapter (3): The Fundamental Sources of Fiqh. Section Three: Ijma'. 4/3 - Ijma' is the agreement of the mujtahid jurists of an era upon a ruling. There is no difference whether these agreeing ones are from the jurists among the Companions of the Messenger (peace and blessings be upon him) after his death or from the later generations. Ijma' is a strong proof in establishing juristic rulings, and a source that follows the Sunnah in rank. The evidence for its consideration in this status as a source of legislation is a set of verses and hadiths that indicate that the agreement of the people of knowledge and opinion is a proof. Among those proofs for considering Ijma' is the saying of Allah the Blessed and Exalted: {And whoever opposes the Messenger after the guidance has become clear to him and follows other than the way of the believers - We will give him what he has taken and drive him into Hell, and evil it is as a destination} (Surah an-Nisa 4:115), and his saying (peace be upon him): 'My community will not unite upon error' (1) and many hadiths to its meaning. By their mutual reinforcement with each other and with the Quranic verses that command adherence to the group and not splitting from it, they constitute sufficient evidence for the authority of Ijma' in establishing rulings. Ijma' in itself, if it is concluded upon a ruling, must be based upon a proof in it, even if the proof is not transmitted with it, for it is inconceivable that the word of the trusted scholars of the community would unite whimsically without a legal proof. Therefore, if later scholars wish to know Ijma', they only search for (1) Reported by Abu Dawud from the hadith of Abu Malik al-Ash'ari (4253), and al-Tirmidhi from the hadith of Ibn Umar (2167) and said: gharib from this chain, and Ibn Majah from the hadith of Anas (3950) with a weak chain, but overall the hadith, as al-Hafiz said in al-Talkhis (3/141): a well-known hadith with many chains, none of which are free from criticism. And al-Sakhawi said in al-Maqasid p.460: overall it is a well-known hadith in text, with many chains, and good supporting evidence in marfu' and other reports.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage defines Ijma' as the agreement of all mujtahid jurists of any era on a ruling, including Companions and later scholars. It affirms Ijma' as a binding proof (hujja) and a source after the Sunnah in rank. The proof for its authority is derived from the Quranic verse (4:115) that condemns following 'other than the way of the believers,' and the hadith 'My community will not unite upon error,' along with other similar hadiths. These collectively establish the authority of consensus. Importantly, the author stresses that Ijma' must be based on a legal proof (dalil), even if that proof is not explicitly transmitted with the consensus; it is inconceivable that all scholars would agree baselessly. Later scholars seeking to ascertain Ijma' investigate the existence of such underlying evidence.

Key Terms
الإجماع (al-Ijma'): The agreement of all mujtahid jurists of a particular era upon a Shar'i ruling.
المجتهدين (al-mujtahidin): Jurists qualified to perform independent legal reasoning (ijtihad) to derive rulings from the primary sources.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what constitutes the primary evidence for the authority of Ijma'?
A) A single hadith only
B) The Quranic verse (4:115) and multiple hadiths together
C) Rational argument alone
D) The practice of the Companions without textual proof

Key Takeaway
Ijma' is a binding source after the Sunnah, defined as unanimous agreement of all mujtahids of an era based on a legal proof, even if the proof is not explicitly transmitted.

Legal Philosophy and Theory
beginner
6 min
Definition and Authority of Ijma' (Consensus)
Defining ijma' and establishing its authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ijma', identify its evidentiary basis from Quran and Sunnah, and apply the condition that ijma' must be based on a shari'i proof.

Core Idea
Ijma' is a binding source of law only when it rests on a shari'i proof, even if that proof is not explicitly transmitted.

This passage introduces ijma' as the third primary source of Islamic jurisprudence after the Qur'an and Sunnah. The author, Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, defines it as the agreement of all mujtahid jurists of an era, and then establishes its authority using Quranic verses and hadith. Importantly, he clarifies that every valid ijma' must be based on a shari'i proof, but when verifying an existing ijma', scholars need only confirm its transmission, not the underlying evidence.

Guided Path
1
Define the term and its scope
Understand that ijma' is the consensus of all mujtahids in a given era, including both Companions and later generations.
2
Identify the proofs for its authority
Locate the Quranic verse (4:115) and the hadith 'My community will not unite upon error' and understand how they collectively establish ijma' as a proof.
The hadith has multiple chains; even if individually weak, together they strengthen the proof.
3
Examine the condition of a supporting proof
Recognize that every ijma' must be based on a shari'i evidence, but when verifying an existing ijma', one need not know that evidence.
Otherwise, the proof would be the evidence, not the consensus itself.
4
Apply to examples
Review the three examples: grandfather's inheritance with son, blockage of siblings by father, and validity of istisna'. Understand how each is an instance of ijma' based on underlying proofs.
These illustrate that ijma' is a practical source of rulings.

الفصل (۳) المصادر الأساسية للفقه
المبحث الثالث: الإجماع
٤/٣ - الإجماع هو اتفاق الفقهاء المجتهدين في عصر على حكم. ولا فرق بين أن يكون هؤلاء المتفقون من فقهاء صحابة الرسول عليه الصلاة والسلام بعد وفاته أو من الطبقات التي جاءت بعدهم. والإجماع حُجَّة قوية في إثبات الأحكام الفقهية، ومصدر يلي السنة في الرتبة.
ودليل اعتباره في هذه المكانة من مصدرية التشريع مجموعة آيات وأحاديث تدل على اعتبار إجماع الكلمة من أهل العلم والرأي حجة. فمن تلك الأدلة على اعتبار الإجماع قول الله تبارك وتعالى: ﴿وَمَن يُشَاقِقِ الرَّسُولَ مِنْ بَعْدِ مَا تَبَيَّنَ لَهُ الْهُدَى وَيَتَّبِعْ غَيْرَ سَبِيلِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ نُوَلِهِ مَا تَوَلَّى وَنُصْلِهِ جَهَنَّمَ وَسَاءَتْ مَصِيرًا﴾ سورة النساء / ١١٥، وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «لا تجتمع أمتي على الضلالة» (1) وفي معناه أحاديث كثيرة. فبتضافرها بعضها مع بعض ومع الآيات القرآنية التي تأمر بلزوم الجماعة وعدم الانشقاق عنها، تؤلف دليلاً كافياً في حجية الإجماع في إثبات الأحكام.
والإجماع في ذاته إذا انعقد على حكم لا بد أن يكون مستنداً إلى دليل فيه، وإن لم ينقل الدليل معه، إذ لا يعقل أن تجتمع كلمة علماء الأمة تشهياً بلا دليل شرعي.

الباب الثاني: مصادر الفقه الإسلامي
ولذلك كان الإجماع إذا أراد المتأخرون معرفته إنما يبحثون عن وجوده وصحة نقله لا عن دليله إذ لو وجب البحث عن دليله لكانت العبرة للدليل لا للإجماع، بينما هو في ذاته حجة.
والخلاصة أنه لا يخلو الإجماع عن دليل يستند إليه، ولكن لا يعتبر لاعتباره أن يكون دليله منقولاً معه ومعروفاً.
ومن أمثلة ثبوت الحكم بالإجماع ميراث الجد مع الابن فيما لو توفي شخص عن ابن وعن جد، فإنَّ الجد عند عدم الأب يحل محل الأب في الإرث، فيرث - مع وجود ابن المتوفى - سدس المال كالأب ثبت ذلك بإجماع الصحابة.
-
وكذا حَجْبُ بني الأعيان والعلات ذكوراً وإناثاً بالأب) (1)
وكذا صحة عقد الاستصناع، فقد انعقد عليها الإجماع (۲)

(1) أخرجه أبو داود من حديث أبي مالك الأشعري (٤٢٥٣)، والترمذي من حديث ابن عمر (٢١٦٧) وقال: غريب من هذا الوجه وابن ماجه من حديث أنس (٣٩٥٠) بإسناد ضعيف، وبالجملة فالحديث كما قال الحافظ في التلخيص ١٤١/٣: حديث مشهور له طرق كثيرة، لا يخلو واحد منها من مقال وقال السخاوي في المقاصد ص ٤٦٠: وبالجملة فهو حديث مشهور، المتن ذو أسانيد كثيرة، وشواهد متعددة في المرفوع وغيره.

(1) ر: أصول الفقه للخضري ص / ٤٠٤/، وشرح السراجية للسيد الجرجاني مقاسمة الجد. وبنو الأعيان هم الإخوة والأخوات لأب وأم. وبنو العلات (بفتح العين وتشديد اللام) هم الإخوة والأخوات لأب. وبنو الأخياف الأخوة والأخوات لأم.
(۲) الاستصناع شراء ما سيُصنع قبل صنعه والقواعد تأباه لأنه بيع المعدوم، ولكن وقع الإجماع على صحته للحاجة إليه (ر): أصول فخر الإسلام البزدوي أول باب الاستحسان.
Chapter (3): The Basic Sources of Fiqh. Third Section: Ijma'. 4/3 - Ijma' is the agreement of the mujtahid fuqaha of an era upon a ruling. There is no difference whether those agreeing are from the fuqaha of the Companions of the Messenger, peace and blessings be upon him, after his death, or from the generations that came after them. Ijma' is a strong proof in establishing fiqh rulings, and a source that follows the Sunnah in rank. The evidence for its consideration in this status as a source of legislation is a group of verses and hadiths that indicate that the consensus of the people of knowledge and opinion is a proof. Among those evidences for considering ijma' is the saying of Allah, Blessed and Exalted: {And whoever opposes the Messenger after guidance has become clear to him and follows other than the way of the believers - We will give him what he has taken and drive him into Hell, and evil is the destination} [Surah an-Nisa, 4:115], and his saying, peace be upon him: 'My community will not unite upon error.' (1) And there are many hadiths with the same meaning. So their conjunction with each other and with the Quranic verses that command adherence to the community and not splitting from it constitute sufficient evidence for the authority of ijma' in establishing rulings. Ijma' in itself, when it occurs upon a ruling, must be based on a proof in it, even if the proof is not transmitted with it, for it is inconceivable that the word of the scholars of the community would unite capriciously without a shari'i proof. The Second Book: Sources of Islamic Fiqh. Therefore, if later ones want to know ijma', they only search for its existence and the correctness of its transmission, not for its proof, for if it were necessary to search for its proof, the consideration would be for the proof, not for ijma', while it is in itself a proof. The conclusion is that ijma' is never devoid of a proof it relies on, but it is not required for its validity that its proof be transmitted with it and known. Among examples of the establishment of a ruling by ijma' is the inheritance of the grandfather with the son: if a person dies leaving a son and a grandfather, then the grandfather, in the absence of the father, takes the place of the father in inheritance, so he inherits - with the existence of the deceased's son - one-sixth of the estate like the father; this was established by the ijma' of the Companions. Similarly, the blockage of banu al-a'yan and banu al-'illat, male and female, by the father (1). And similarly, the validity of the contract of istisna', for ijma' has occurred upon it (2). Footnote (1): Reported by Abu Dawud from Abu Malik al-Ash'ari (4253), al-Tirmidhi from Ibn 'Umar (2167) and said: gharib from this chain, and Ibn Majah from Anas (3950) with a weak chain. Overall, the hadith as al-Hafiz said in al-Talkhis (3/141): a famous hadith with many chains, none of which are free from criticism. And al-Sakhawi said in al-Maqasid p.460: Overall, it is a famous hadith in wording with many chains and multiple supporting evidences in marfu' and other. Footnote (1): Ref: Usul al-Fiqh by al-Khudari p. 404, and Sharh al-Sirajiyya by al-Sayyid al-Jurjani on the division of the grandfather. Banu al-a'yan are full brothers and sisters. Banu al-'illat (with fath on 'ayn and tashdid on lam) are consanguine brothers and sisters. Banu al-akhyaf are uterine brothers and sisters. Footnote (2): Istisna' is the purchase of something to be manufactured before its manufacture, and the rules reject it because it is a sale of a non-existent thing, but ijma' has occurred upon its validity due to necessity. Ref: Usul Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, beginning of the chapter on istihsan.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is a legal philosophy text defining the concept of ijma' (consensus) and establishing its authority as a source of fiqh. The author, Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, begins by defining ijma' as the agreement of all mujtahid jurists in a given era upon a specific ruling. He emphasizes that this consensus includes both the Companions and later generations. The authority of ijma' is ranked after the Qur'an and Sunnah, meaning it is a secondary source but still binding. To support his claim, he cites Quranic verse 4:115, which threatens those who follow a path other than that of the believers, and the hadith 'My community will not unite upon error,' noting that even if some chains are weak, the multiple narrations strengthen it. Importantly, al-Zarqa asserts that every valid ijma' must be based on a shari'i proof; it cannot be mere speculation without evidence. However, when later scholars investigate an ijma', they need only verify its transmission, not necessarily its underlying proof, because the consensus itself is a proof. He then provides three classical examples of rulings established by ijma': (1) the grandfather inheriting one-sixth in the presence of the son, based on the ijma' of the Companions; (2) the blocking of full and consanguine siblings by the father; and (3) the validity of istisna' contracts (manufacturing contracts), which contradict general sales principles but are permitted by consensus due to necessity.

Key Terms
الإجماع (al-ijmāʿ): اتفاق الفقهاء المجتهدين في عصر على حكم
حجة (ḥujjah): دليل معتبر يثبت به الحكم
الجد (al-jadd): أبو الأب
بنو الأعيان (banū al-aʿyān): الإخوة والأخوات لأب وأم
الاستصناع (al-istiṣnāʿ): عقد على شيء سيصنع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for an ijma' to be valid?
A) All mujtahids must explicitly agree
B) It must be based on a shari'i proof
C) It must be transmitted from the Sahaba
D) It must be approved by the public

Key Takeaway
Every valid ijma' is anchored in a shari'i proof, but the proof itself need not be transmitted; the consensus as transmitted is itself a sufficient proof.
